***willkommen.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a> (85978)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle High German">Middle High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmh">willekomen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_High_German" class="extiw" title="w:Old High German">Old High German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="goh">willechomen</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*wiljakumô</i>. Cognate to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:welkom.html>welkom</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">welcome</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Danish language">Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="da">velkommen</i>, and other Germanic forms. Compare also <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr">bienvenu</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_language" class="extiw" title="w:Italian language">Italian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="it">benvenuto</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Spanish language">Spanish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="es">bienvenido</i>, possibly Germanic calques.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjective">Adjective</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>welcome <span class="gloss-brac">(</span><span class="gloss-content">received with gladness</span><span class="gloss-brac">)</span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de">Du <a href = vnd.unilang:bist.html>bist</a> mir <a href = vnd.unilang:immer.html>immer</a> <b><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></b>.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">You’re always <b>welcome</b> to my house.</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:das.html>Das</a> ist eine <b>willkommene</b> Gelegenheit.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">This <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a <b>welcome</b> opportunity.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li>The German word <i>gern</i> can translate English welcome in some constructions.  This <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> not used with a following infinitive; to say “You are welcome to use my car", use a sentence such as <i>Du kannst gern <a href = vnd.unilang:mein.html>mein</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:auto.html>Auto</a> nehmen.</i></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_terms">Derived <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a> heißen</span></li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interjection">Interjection</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></strong>
</p>
<ol><li>welcome
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a></b> in Deutschland!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation"><b>Welcome</b> to Germany!</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a></b> am Bodensee!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation"><b>Welcome</b> to Lake <a href = vnd.unilang:constance.html>Constance</a>!</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a></b> auf Helgoland!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation"><b>Welcome</b> to Heligoland!</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a></b> auf meiner Webseite!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation"><b>Welcome</b> to my website!</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="de"><b><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:bei.html>bei</a> meinen Eltern!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation"><b>Welcome</b> to my parents’ house!</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage_notes_2">Usage notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li>As can be seen from the examples above, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> construed with prepositions of position (not movement) corresponding to the object. Thus, <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">in</i> with countries and cities, <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">an</i> with <a href = vnd.unilang:bodies.html>bodies</a> of water, <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:bei.html>bei</a></i> with people, etc., as they are generally used to indicate position.</li>
<li>The preposition <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">zu</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> may be used with events and activities: <i><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a> zur Weinprobe!</i> (“Welcome to the winetasting!”) However, one may also follow the general rule and use <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:bei.html>bei</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">auf</i>, or whatever preposition of position <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> appropriate.</li></ul>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<ul><li><strong class="Latn headword" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></strong> (<i>class 4 strong</i>, <i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de">willkommt</b>, <i>past tense</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de">willkam</b>, <i>past participle</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de"><strong class="selflink"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></strong></b>, <i>past subjunctive</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de">willkäme</b>, <i>auxiliary</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:haben.html>haben</a></b>)</li>
<li><strong class="Latn headword" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>willkommen</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de">willkommt</b>, <i>past tense</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de">willkommte</b>, <i>past participle</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de">willkommt/gewillkommt</b>, <i>auxiliary</i> <b class="Latn" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:haben.html>haben</a></b>)</li></ul>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> to welcome</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_terms">Related <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:willkommen.html>Willkommen</a></span></li></ul>
</body> 
***willow.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:willow.html>willow</a> (7756)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">wilwe</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">welew</i>, variant of <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">wilghe</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">weliġ</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*wiligaz</i> (compare <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Frisian_language" class="extiw" title="w:West Frisian language">West Frisian</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fy">wylch</i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wilg.html>wilg</a></i>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*wel-ik-</i> (compare (Arcadian) <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">ἑλίκη</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">helíkē</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hittite_language" class="extiw" title="w:Hittite language">Hittite</a></span> <i class="Xsux mention" lang="hit">𒌑𒂖𒆪</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="hit-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">welku</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">grass</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>), from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ine-pro">*wel-</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">twist, turn</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:willow.html>willow</a></strong> (<i>countable and uncountable</i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">willows</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Any of various deciduous trees or shrubs in the genus <i>Salix</i>, in the <a href = vnd.unilang:willow.html>willow</a> family Salicaceae, found primarily on moist soils in cooler <a href = vnd.unilang:zones.html>zones</a> in the northern hemisphere.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1912</b> January,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zane_Grey" class="extiw" title="w:Zane Grey"><a href = vnd.unilang:zane.html>Zane</a> Grey</a>,  chapter 8, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Riders_of_the_Purple_Sage" class="extiw" title="w:Riders of the Purple Sage"><a href = vnd.unilang:riders.html>Riders</a> of the Purple Sage: A Novel</a></cite>, New York, N.Y.; London |  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harper_(publisher)" class="extiw" title="w:Harper (publisher)">Harper amp; Brothers Publishers</a>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/6868219">6868219</a></small>:</span><dl><dd></dd></dl></div>
<dl><dd><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="Instead there were the white of aspens, streaks of branch and slender trunk glistening from the green of leaves, and the darker green of oaks,">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> and through the middle of this forest, from wall to wall, <a href = vnd.unilang:ran.html>ran</a> a <a href = vnd.unilang:winding.html>winding</a> line of brilliant green which marked the course of cottonwoods and <b>willows</b>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>The wood of these trees.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">cricket<span class="ib-comma">,</span> colloquial</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A cricket bat.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">baseball<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> 1800s</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The baseball bat.</li>
<li>A rotating spiked drum used to open and clean cotton heads.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<ul><li><span class="Latn" lang="en">withy</span></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_terms">Derived <a href = vnd.unilang:terms.html>terms</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:willow.html>willow</a></strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">willows</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">willowing</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">willowed</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To open and cleanse (cotton, flax, wool, etc.) by means of a <a href = vnd.unilang:willow.html>willow</a>.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">intransitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To form a shape or move in a way similar to the long, slender <a href = vnd.unilang:branches.html>branches</a> of a <a href = vnd.unilang:willow.html>willow</a>.
<ul><li><b>1928</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Byron" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Robert Byron">Robert Byron</a>, <i>The Station: Travels to the Holy Mountain of Greece</i>, Chapter 12,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.gutenberg.net.au/ebooks14/1403311h.html">[1]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><b>Willowing</b> <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> the rough cobbles of the little <a href = vnd.unilang:pier.html>pier</a> stepped a thin, <a href = vnd.unilang:bent.html>bent</a> figure, adorned with a silver nannygoat’s beard and bobbling <a href = vnd.unilang:eyes.html>eyes</a> interrupted by the rim of a pair of pince-nez.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1930</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talbot_Mundy" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Talbot Mundy"><a href = vnd.unilang:talbot.html>Talbot</a> Mundy</a>, <i>Black Light</i>, Chapter 7,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://gutenberg.net.au/ebooks06/0609211h.html">[2]</a></sup>
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:joe.html>Joe</a>’s impulse <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> to sketch her, with her shadow <b>willowing</b> beyond her on the mouse-gray paving-stone; but his left fist, obeying <a href = vnd.unilang:instinct.html>instinct</a>, remained clenched behind his back <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1985</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Booth" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Martin Booth">Martin Booth</a>, <i>Hiroshima <a href = vnd.unilang:joe.html>Joe</a></i>, New York: Picador, p. 394,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.ca/books?id=lYXWAAAAQBAJamp;printsec=frontcoverv=onepageamp;qamp;f=false">[3]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>It <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> floating a foot under the surface. The <a href = vnd.unilang:eyes.html>eyes</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:holes.html>holes</a>. The mouth <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> a slit cavern of darkness. The hair <b>willowed</b> around the scalp.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2013</b>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dean_Koontz" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Dean Koontz"><a href = vnd.unilang:dean.html>Dean</a> Koontz</a>, <i>Wilderness</i>, Bantam Books,<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.ca/books?id=sVE0AQAAQBAJamp;printsec=frontcoverv=onepageamp;qamp;f=false">[4]</a></sup>
<dl><dd>The draft-drawn smoke <b>willowed</b> down through the hole and across my face, but I didn’<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> worry about coughing or sneezing.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<ul><li>Originally northern British usage, from the 1960s. Probably the simple use of a proper name as a pet name; compare <i><a href = vnd.unilang:dick.html>dick</a></i>, <i><a href = vnd.unilang:fanny.html>fanny</a></i> and <i><a href = vnd.unilang:peter.html>peter</a></i>. Unlikely to be a contraction of <span class="etylcleanup"><span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a></span></span> <i>membrum virile</i>, male member (that <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a>, the <a href = vnd.unilang:penis.html>penis</a>), a Latin term used in English in the nineteenth century.</li></ul>

</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">hypocoristic<span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> childish</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> the <a href = vnd.unilang:penis.html>penis</a>.</li>

***wimper.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:wimper.html>wimper</a> (52683)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Dutch">Middle Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">wimbrauw</i>, contraction of <i class="Latn mention" lang="dum">wintbrauwe</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Dutch" class="extiw" title="w:Old Dutch">Old Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="odt">*wintbrāwa</i>. The first element <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> unknown but presumed to be related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="w:Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a></span> <i class="polytonic mention" lang="grc">ἴονθος</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="grc-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">íonthos</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>; the second element <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*brēwō</i>. Doublet of <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wenkbrauw.html>wenkbrauw</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">eyebrow</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. The form <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wimper.html>wimper</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> native in some Dutch dialects; its adoption into the standard language (19th c.) probably under influence of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href = vnd.unilang:wimper.html>Wimper</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wimper.html>wimper</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wimpers.html>wimpers</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:wimper.html>wimpertje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>
<ol><li>eyelash</li></ol>

<p><b><a href = vnd.unilang:wimper.html>wimper</a></b> <span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic">v</span>/<span style="background-color: f8f9fa;border-radius: 2px;border: 1px solid c8ccd1;padding: 0 0.2em 0 0.1em;font-style: italic">m</span>
